TITLE: Andreessen Horowitz moves out of Delaware, citing state's legal 'bias'Also known as A16z, the firm said it could have made the move quietly but felt it was important for its 
stakeholders and the broader tech and VC communities to understand the reasons behind the decision, and also suggested its portfolio companies to consider making similar moves.  
Delaware's Court of Chancery, which had "injected an unprecedented level of subjectivity into judicial decisions, undermining the court's reputation for unbiased expertise", had caused
legal uncertainty, A16z, which has been an early backer in some of today's hottest AI companies, including Databricks and Elon Musk's xAI, said.
